--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-652x-xj99-gmcc
Package: requests
Summary: Exposure of Sensitive Information to an Unauthorized Actor in Requests
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=0, <2.3.0
Fix Version: 2.3.0
Details: Requests (aka python-requests) before 2.3.0 allows remote servers to obtain sensitive information by reading the Proxy-Authorization header in a redirected request.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-9hjg-9r4m-mvj7
Package: requests
Summary: Requests vulnerable to .netrc credentials leak via malicious URLs
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Affected Versions: >=0, <2.32.4
Fix Version: 2.32.4
Details: ### Impact

Due to a URL parsing issue, Requests releases prior to 2.32.4 may leak .netrc credentials to third parties for specific maliciously-crafted URLs.

### Workarounds
For older versions of Requests, use of the .netrc file can be disabled with `trust_env=False` on your Requests Session ([docs](https://requests.readthedocs.io/en/latest/api/#requests.Session.trust_env)).

### References
https://github.com/psf/requests/pull/6965
https://seclists.org/fulldisclosure/2025/Jun/2
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

Advisory ID: GHSA-j8r2-6x86-q33q
Package: requests
Summary: Unintended leak of Proxy-Authorization header in requests
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:H/I:N/A:N
Affected Versions: >=2.3.0, <2.31.0
Fix Version: 2.31.0
Details: ### Impact

Since Requests v2.3.0, Requests has been vulnerable to potentially leaking `Proxy-Authorization` headers to destination servers, specifically during redirects to an HTTPS origin. This is a product of how `rebuild_proxies` is used to recompute and [reattach the `Proxy-Authorization` header](https://github.com/psf/requests/blob/f2629e9e3c7ce3c3c8c025bcd8db551101cbc773/requests/sessions.py#L319-L328) to requests when redirected. Note this behavior has _only_ been observed to affect prox
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

Advisory ID: GHSA-x84v-xcm2-53pg
Package: requests
Summary: Insufficiently Protected Credentials in Requests
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Affected Versions: >=0, <2.20.0
Fix Version: 2.20.0

This is a product of how we use `rebuild_proxies` to reattach the `Proxy-Authorization` header to requests. For HTTP connections sent through the tunnel, the proxy will identify the header in the request itself and remove it prior to forwarding to the destination server. Package: flask
Summary: Flask uses fallback key instead of current signing key
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=3.1.0, <3.1.1
Fix Version: 3.1.1
Details: In Flask 3.1.0, the way fallback key configuration was handled resulted in the last fallback key being used for signing, rather than the current signing key.

Signing is provided by the `itsdangerous` library. A list of keys can be passed, and it expects the last (top) key in the list to be the most recent key, and uses that for signing. Flask was incorrectly constructing that list in reverse, passing the signing key first.

--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

Advisory ID: GHSA-2f9x-5v75-3qv4
Package: django
Summary: Django Denial-of-service possibility in truncatechars_html and truncatewords_html template filters
Severity: CVSS:3.0/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:N/A:L
Affected Versions: >=2.0, <2.0.3, >=1.11, <1.11.11, >=1.8, <1.8.19
Fix Version: 1.8.19
Details: An issue was discovered in Django 2.0 before 2.0.3, 1.11 before 1.11.11, and 1.8 before 1.8.19. If django.utils.text.Truncator's chars() and words() methods were passed the html=True argument, they were extremely slow to evaluate certain inputs due to a catastrophic backtracking vulnerability in a regular expression. The chars() and words() methods are used to implement the truncatechars_html and truncatewords_html template filters, which were thus vulnerable.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-37hp-765x-j95x
Package: django
Summary: Django open redirect and possible XSS attack via user-supplied numeric redirect URLs
Severity: CVSS:3.0/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N
Affected Versions: >=1.10a1, <1.10.7, >=1.9a1, <1.9.13, >=1.8a1, <1.8.18
Fix Version: 1.8.18
Details: Django 1.10 before 1.10.7, 1.9 before 1.9.13, and 1.8 before 1.8.18 relies on user input in some cases to redirect the user to an "on success" URL. The security check for these redirects (namely ``django.utils.http.is_safe_url()``) considered some numeric URLs "safe" when they shouldn't be, aka an open redirect vulnerability. Also, if a developer relies on ``is_safe_url()`` to provide safe redirect targets and puts such a URL into a link, they could suffer from an XSS attack.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

Summary: Django has a Race Condition vulnerability
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:L/I:N/A:N

Race condition in file-system storage and file-based cache backends in Django allows an attacker to cause file system objects to be created with incorrect permissions via concurrent requests, where one thread's temporary `umask` change affects other threads in multi-threaded environments.

`FilteredRelation` is subject to SQL injection in column aliases, using a suitably crafted dictionary, with dictionary expansion, as the `**kwargs` passed to `QuerySet.annotate()` or `QuerySet.alias()` on PostgreSQL.
Earlier, unsupported Django series (such as 5.0.x, 4.1.x, and 3.2.x) were not evaluated and may also be affected.
Django would like to thank Stackered for reporting this issue.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

Advisory ID: GHSA-wxg3-mfph-qg9w
Package: django
Summary: Django Might Allow CSRF Requests via URL Verification
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:H/A:N
Affected Versions: >=0, <1.2.7, >=1.3, <1.3.1
Fix Version: 1.3.1
Details: The `verify_exists` functionality in the URLField implementation in Django before 1.2.7 and 1.3.x before 1.3.1 originally tests a URL's validity through a HEAD request, but then uses a GET request for the new target URL in the case of a redirect, which might allow remote attackers to trigger arbitrary GET requests with an unintended source IP address via a crafted Location header.

Package: django
Summary: No summary available

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: PYSEC-2017-9
Package: django
Summary: No summary available
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=1.8, <1.8.18
Fix Version: 1.8.18
Details: Django 1.10 before 1.10.7, 1.9 before 1.9.13, and 1.8 before 1.8.18 relies on user input in some cases to redirect the user to an "on success" URL. The security check for these redirects (namely ``django.utils.http.is_safe_url()``) considered some numeric URLs "safe" when they shouldn't be, aka an open redirect vulnerability. Also, if a developer relies on ``is_safe_url()`` to provide safe redirect targets and puts such a URL into a link, they could suffer from an XSS attack.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: PYSEC-2018-3
Package: django
Summary: No summary available
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=2.1, <2.1.2
Fix Version: 2.1.2
Details: An issue was discovered in Django 2.1 before 2.1.2, in which unprivileged users can read the password hashes of arbitrary accounts. The read-only password widget used by the Django Admin to display an obfuscated password hash was bypassed if a user has only the "view" permission (new in Django 2.1), resulting in display of the entire password hash to those users. This may result in a vulnerability for sites with legacy user accounts using insecure hashes.

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: PYSEC-2018-5
Package: django
Summary: No summary available
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=2.0, <2.0.3
Fix Version: 2.0.3
Details: An issue was discovered in Django 2.0 before 2.0.3, 1.11 before 1.11.11, and 1.8 before 1.8.19. The django.utils.html.urlize() function was extremely slow to evaluate certain inputs due to catastrophic backtracking vulnerabilities in two regular expressions (only one regular expression for Django 1.8.x). The urlize() function is used to implement the urlize and urlizetrunc template filters, which were thus vulnerable.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: PYSEC-2018-6
Package: django
Summary: No summary available
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=2.0, <2.0.3
Fix Version: 2.0.3
Details: An issue was discovered in Django 2.0 before 2.0.3, 1.11 before 1.11.11, and 1.8 before 1.8.19. If django.utils.text.Truncator's chars() and words() methods were passed the html=True argument, they were extremely slow to evaluate certain inputs due to a catastrophic backtracking vulnerability in a regular expression. The chars() and words() methods are used to implement the truncatechars_html and truncatewords_html template filters, which were thus vulnerable.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

Affected Versions: >=1.11, <1.11.22

Details: An issue was discovered in Django 1.11 before 1.11.22, 2.1 before 2.1.10, and 2.2 before 2.2.3. Summary: Pillow affected by out-of-bounds write when loading PSD images
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=10.3.0, <12.1.1
Fix Version: 12.1.1
Details: ### Impact
An out-of-bounds write may be triggered when loading a specially crafted PSD image. Pillow >= 10.3.0 users are affected.

### Patches
Pillow 12.1.1 will be released shortly with a fix for this.

`Image.open()` has a `formats` parameter that can be used to prevent PSD images from being opened.

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-hr8g-f6r6-mr22
Package: pillow
Summary: Buffer over-flow in Pillow
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:N/A:H
Affected Versions: >=9.1.0, <9.1.1
Fix Version: 9.1.1
Details: When reading a TGA file with RLE packets that cross scan lines, Pillow reads the information past the end of the first line without deducting that from the length of the remaining file data. This vulnerability was introduced in Pillow 9.1.0, and can cause a heap buffer overflow.

Opening an image with a zero or negative height has been found to bypass a decompression bomb check. This will now raise a SyntaxError instead, in turn raising a PIL.UnidentifiedImageError.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

Advisory ID: GHSA-q5hq-fp76-qmrc
Package: pillow
Summary: Uncontrolled Resource Consumption in Pillow
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:N/A:H
Affected Versions: >=0, <8.2.0
Fix Version: 8.2.0
Details: An issue was discovered in Pillow before 8.2.0. For EPS data, the readline implementation used in EPSImageFile has to deal with any combination of \r and \n as line endings. It used an accidentally quadratic method of accumulating lines while looking for a line ending. A malicious EPS file could use this to perform a DoS of Pillow in the open phase, before an image was accepted for opening.

Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=0, <6.2.2
Fix Version: 6.2.2

Advisory ID: GHSA-q4xr-rc97-m4xx
Package: celery
Summary: OS Command Injection in celery
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:H
Affected Versions: >=0, <5.2.2
Fix Version: 5.2.2
Details: This affects the package celery before 5.2.2. It by default trusts the messages and metadata stored in backends (result stores). When reading task metadata from the backend, the data is deserialized. Given that an attacker can gain access to, or somehow manipulate the metadata within a celery backend, they could trigger a stored command injection vulnerability and potentially gain further access to the system.

Advisory ID: GHSA-6vqw-3v5j-54x4
Package: cryptography
Summary: cryptography NULL pointer dereference with pkcs12.serialize_key_and_certificates when called with a non-matching certificate and private key and an hmac_hash override
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:N/A:H
Affected Versions: >=38.0.0, <42.0.4
Fix Version: 42.0.4
Details: If `pkcs12.serialize_key_and_certificates` is called with both:

1. A certificate whose public key did not match the provided private key
2. An `encryption_algorithm` with `hmac_hash` set (via `PrivateFormat.PKCS12.encryption_builder().hmac_hash(...)`

Then a NULL pointer dereference would occur, crashing the Python process.

This has been resolved, and now a `ValueError` is properly raised.

Patched in https://github.com/pyca/cryptography/pull/10423
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

Advisory ID: GHSA-fcf9-3qw3-gxmj
Package: cryptography
Summary: PyCA Cryptography vulnerable to GCM tag forgery
Severity: CVSS:3.0/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Affected Versions: >=1.9.0, <2.3
Fix Version: 2.3
Details: A flaw was found in python-cryptography versions between >=1.9.0 and <2.3. The finalize_with_tag API did not enforce a minimum tag length. If a user did not validate the input length prior to passing it to finalize_with_tag an attacker could craft an invalid payload with a shortened tag (e.g. 1 byte) such that they would have a 1 in 256 chance of passing the MAC check. GCM tag forgeries can cause key leakage.

Terrapin is a prefix truncation attack targeting the SSH protocol. More precisely, Terrapin breaks the integrity of SSH's secure channel. By carefully adjusting the sequence numbers during the handshake, an attacker can remove an arbitrary amount of messages sent by the client or server at the beginning of the secure channel without the client or server noticing it.

Package: werkzeug
Summary: Werkzeug safe_join not safe on Windows
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=0, <3.0.6
Fix Version: 3.0.6

Werkzeug's `safe_join()` relies on this check, and so can produce a path that is not safe, potentially allowing unintended access to data. Advisory ID: GHSA-hgf8-39gv-g3f2
Package: werkzeug

Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=0, <3.1.4
Fix Version: 3.1.4
Details: Werkzeug's `safe_join` function allows path segments with Windows device names. Advisory ID: GHSA-gm62-xv2j-4w53
Package: urllib3
Summary: urllib3 allows an unbounded number of links in the decompression chain
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=1.24, <2.6.0
Fix Version: 2.6.0
Details: ## Impact

urllib3 supports chained HTTP encoding algorithms for response content according to RFC 9110 (e.g., `Content-Encoding: gzip, zstd`).

However, the number of links in the decompression chain was unbounded allowing a malicious server to insert a virtually unlimited number of compression steps leading to high CPU usage and massive memory allocation for the decompressed data.

Package: aiohttp

Affected Versions: >=3.10.6, <3.10.11
Fix Version: 3.10.11
Details: ### Summary

A memory leak can occur when a request produces a `MatchInfoError`. This was caused by adding an entry to a cache on each request, due to the building of each `MatchInfoError` producing a unique cache entry.

### Impact

If the user is making use of any middlewares with `aiohttp.web` then it is advisable to upgrade immediately.

An attacker may be able to exhaust the memory resources of a server by sending a substantial number (100,000s to millions) of such requests.

Affected Versions: >=0, <3.8.6
Fix Version: 3.8.6
Details: # Summary
The HTTP parser in AIOHTTP has numerous problems with header parsing, which could lead to request smuggling.
This parser is only used when `AIOHTTP_NO_EXTENSIONS` is enabled (or not using a prebuilt wheel).

Advisory ID: GHSA-jj3x-wxrx-4x23
Package: aiohttp
Summary: AIOHTTP vulnerable to DoS when bypassing asserts
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=0, <3.13.3
Fix Version: 3.13.3
Details: ### Summary
When assert statements are bypassed, an infinite loop can occur, resulting in a DoS attack when processing a POST body.

### Impact
If optimisations are enabled (`-O` or `PYTHONOPTIMIZE=1`), and the application includes a handler that uses the `Request.post()` method, then an attacker may be able to execute a DoS attack with a specially crafted message.

Since parsing occurs synchronously on the main thread, this creates the possibility of denial-of-service due to the cost of parsing very large multipart bodies with many parts.

--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

This is known to apply to older versions of haproxy, although the current release is not affected.

Advisory ID: GHSA-cw9j-q3vf-hrrv
Package: scrapy
Summary: Scrapy authorization header leakage on cross-domain redirect
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:N/A:N
Affected Versions: >=2, <2.11.1, >=0, <1.8.4
Fix Version: 1.8.4
Details: ### Impact

When you send a request with the `Authorization` header to one domain, and the response asks to redirect to a different domain, Scrapy’s built-in redirect middleware creates a follow-up redirect request that keeps the original `Authorization` header, leaking its content to that second domain.

The [right behavior](https://fetch.spec.whatwg.org/#ref-for-cors-non-wildcard-request-header-name) would be to drop the `Authorization` header instead, in this scenario.

Upgrade t
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

Fix Version: 4.5.3
Details: redis-py before 4.5.3, as used in ChatGPT and other products, leaves a connection open after canceling an async Redis command at an inopportune time (in the case of a pipeline operation), and can send response data to the client of an unrelated request in an off-by-one manner. The fixed versions for this CVE Record are 4.3.6, 4.4.3, and 4.5.3; however, CVE-2023-28859 is a separate vulnerability.

Fix Version: 2.4.4
Details: ### Impact
If `tf.tile` is called with a large input argument then the TensorFlow process will crash due to a `CHECK`-failure caused by an overflow.

```python

import numpy as np

```

The number of elements in the output tensor is too much for the `int64_t` type and the overflow is detected via a `CHECK` statement. This aborts the process.

Summary: Out of bounds access in tensorflow-lite

Fix Version: 2.3.1
Details: ### Impact
In TensorFlow Lite, saved models in the flatbuffer format use a double indexing scheme: a model has a set of subgraphs, each subgraph has a set of operators and each operator has a set of input/output tensors. The flatbuffer format uses indices for the tensors, indexing into an array of tensors that is owned by the subgraph. This results in a pattern of double array indexing when trying to get the data of each tensor: https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/blob/0e68f4d3295eb0281a517
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

Advisory ID: GHSA-j3mj-fhpq-qqjj
Package: tensorflow
Summary: Reachable Assertion in Tensorflow

Details: ### Impact
When decoding a tensor from protobuf, a TensorFlow process can encounter cases where a `CHECK` assertion is invalidated based on user controlled arguments, if the tensors have an invalid `dtype` and 0 elements or an invalid shape. Advisory ID: GHSA-m539-j985-hcr8
Package: tensorflow
Summary: Crash in `max_pool3d` when size argument is 0 or negative
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:L/AC:L/PR:L/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:N/A:H
Affected Versions: >=2.6.0, <2.6.1, >=2.5.0, <2.5.2, >=0, <2.4.4
Fix Version: 2.4.4
Details: ### Impact
The Keras pooling layers can trigger a segfault if the size of the pool is 0 or if a dimension is negative: 

```python

```

This is due to the TensorFlow's implementation of pooling operations where the values in the sliding window are not checked to be strictly positive.

Advisory ID: GHSA-mw6v-crh8-8533
Package: tensorflow
Summary: Integer Overflow or Wraparound in Google TensorFlow
Severity: CVSS:3.0/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:H
Affected Versions: >=1.0.0, <1.7.1
Fix Version: 1.7.1
Details: ### Issue Description
Google TensorFlow 1.7.x and earlier is affected by a Buffer Overflow vulnerability. The type of exploitation is context-dependent. Newer constructs exist which return a `Status` instead of crashing the binary.

Affected Versions: >=0, <2.5.3, >=2.6.0, <2.6.3, >=2.7.0, <2.7.1
Fix Version: 2.7.1
Details: ### Impact
The [implementation of `AssignOp`](https://github.com/tensorflow/tensorflow/blob/a1320ec1eac186da1d03f033109191f715b2b130/tensorflow/core/kernels/assign_op.h#L30-L143) can result in copying unitialized data to a new tensor. This later results in undefined behavior.

The implementation has a check that the left hand side of the assignment is initialized (to minimize number of allocations), but does not check that the right hand side is also initialized.

--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

Details: ### Impact
In eager mode, TensorFlow does not set the session state. Hence, calling `tf.raw_ops.GetSessionHandle` or `tf.raw_ops.GetSessionHandleV2` results in a null pointer dereference:

In the above snippet, in eager mode, `ctx->session_state()` returns `nullptr`. Since code immediately dereferences this, we get a segmentation fault.

Details: ### Impact

Fix Version: 2.4.4
Details: ### Impact
While calculating the size of the output within the `tf.range` kernel, there is a conditional statement of type `int64 = condition ? int64 : double`. ```python

```python
tf.sparse.eye(num_rows=9223372036854775807, num_columns=None)
```

Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:N/A:L
Affected Versions: >=0, <2.4.0
Fix Version: 2.4.0
Details: ### Impact
When the `boxes` argument of `tf.image.crop_and_resize` has a very large value, the CPU kernel implementation receives it as a C++ `nan` floating point value. Attempting to operate on this is undefined behavior which later produces a segmentation fault.

### Patches

We have patched the issue in c0319231333f0f16e1cc75ec83660b01fedd4182 and will release TensorFlow 2.4.0 containing the patch. TensorFlow nightly packages after this commit will also have the issue resolved.

### For more 
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

Advisory ID: PYSEC-2020-139
Package: tensorflow
Summary: No summary available
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=0, <2.4.0
Fix Version: 2.4.0
Details: In Tensorflow before version 2.4.0, when the `boxes` argument of `tf.image.crop_and_resize` has a very large value, the CPU kernel implementation receives it as a C++ `nan` floating point value. Attempting to operate on this is undefined behavior which later produces a segmentation fault. The issue is patched in eccb7ec454e6617738554a255d77f08e60ee0808 and TensorFlow 2.4.0 will be released containing the patch. TensorFlow nightly packages after this commit will also have the issue resolved.

Advisory ID: PYSEC-2020-140
Package: tensorflow
Summary: No summary available
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=0, <ebc70b7a592420d3d2f359e4b1694c236b82c7ae, >=2.3.0, <2.3.2
Fix Version: 2.3.2
Details: In affected versions of TensorFlow the tf.raw_ops.DataFormatVecPermute API does not validate the src_format and dst_format attributes. The code assumes that these two arguments define a permutation of NHWC. This can result in uninitialized memory accesses, read outside of bounds and even crashes. Package: scikit-learn
Summary: scikit-learn Denial of Service
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:N/A:H

Advisory ID: GHSA-rf74-v2fm-23pw
Package: nltk
Summary: Natural Language Toolkit (NLTK) has unbounded recursion in JSONTaggedDecoder.decode_obj() may cause DoS
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=0
Fix Version: Not specified
Details: ### Summary
`JSONTaggedDecoder.decode_obj()` in `nltk/jsontags.py` calls itself 
recursively without any depth limit. A deeply nested JSON structure 
exceeding `sys.getrecursionlimit()` (default: 1000) will raise an 
unhandled `RecursionError`, crashing the Python process.

        obj = {key: cls.decode_obj(val) for (key, val) in obj.items()}
    elif isinstance

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-55x5-fj6c-h6m8
Package: lxml
Summary: lxml's HTML Cleaner allows crafted and SVG embedded scripts to pass through
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:H/A:N
Affected Versions: >=0, <4.6.5
Fix Version: 4.6.5
Details: ### Impact
The HTML Cleaner in lxml.html lets certain crafted script content pass through, as well as script content in SVG files embedded using data URIs.

Users that employ the HTML cleaner in a security relevant context should upgrade to lxml 4.6.5.

### Patches
The issue has been resolved in lxml 4.6.5.

### Workarounds
None.

### References
The issues are tracked under the report IDs GHSL-2021-1037 and GHSL-2021-1038.

--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-jq4v-f5q6-mjqq
Package: lxml
Summary: lxml vulnerable to Cross-Site Scripting 
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N
Affected Versions: >=0, <4.6.3
Fix Version: 4.6.3
Details: An XSS vulnerability was discovered in the python `lxml` clean module versions before 4.6.3. When disabling `the safe_attrs_only` and `forms` arguments, the `Cleaner` class does not remove the `formaction` attribute allowing for JS to bypass the sanitizer. A remote attacker could exploit this flaw to run arbitrary JS code on users who interact with incorrectly sanitized HTML. This issue is patched in `lxml` 4.6.3.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-pgww-xf46-h92r
Package: lxml
Summary: lxml vulnerable to Cross-site Scripting
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:C/C:L/I:L/A:N
Affected Versions: >=0, <4.6.2
Fix Version: 4.6.2
Details: A XSS vulnerability was discovered in python-lxml's clean module. The module's parser didn't properly imitate browsers, which caused different behaviors between the sanitizer and the user's page. A remote attacker could exploit this flaw to run arbitrary HTML/JS code.

Details: An XSS vulnerability was discovered in python-lxml's clean module versions before 4.6.3. When disabling the safe_attrs_only and forms arguments, the Cleaner class does not remove the formaction attribute allowing for JS to bypass the sanitizer. A remote attacker could exploit this flaw to run arbitrary JS code on users who interact with incorrectly sanitized HTML. This issue is patched in lxml 4.6.3.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-2rcm-phc9-3945
Package: pyopenssl
Summary: Pyopenssl Incorrect Memory Management
Severity: CVSS:3.0/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:N/A:H
Affected Versions: >=0, <17.5.0
Fix Version: 17.5.0
Details: It was discovered that pyOpenSSL incorrectly handled memory when performing operations on a PKCS #12 store. A remote attacker could possibly use this issue to cause pyOpenSSL to consume resources, resulting in a denial of service.

This attack appear to be exploitable via Depends upon calling application, however it could be as simple as initiating a TLS connection that would cause the calling application to reload certificates from a PKCS #12 store. This vulnerability appears to have been fixed
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-5pwr-322w-8jr4
Package: pyopenssl
Summary: pyOpenSSL DTLS cookie callback buffer overflow
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=22.0.0, <26.0.0
Fix Version: 26.0.0
Details: If a user provided callback to `set_cookie_generate_callback` returned a cookie value greater than 256 bytes, pyOpenSSL would overflow an OpenSSL provided buffer.

Cookie values that are too long are now rejected.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-6748-36qp-fx6r
Package: pyopenssl
Summary: PyOpenSSL Mishandles NUL Byte In Certificate Subject Alternative Name
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:H/A:N
Affected Versions: >=0, <0.13.1
Fix Version: 0.13.1
Details: The X509Extension in pyOpenSSL before 0.13.1 does not properly handle a `\0` character in a domain name in the Subject Alternative Name field of an X.509 certificate, which allows man-in-the-middle attackers to spoof arbitrary SSL servers via a crafted certificate issued by a legitimate Certification Authority.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-p28m-34f6-967q
Package: pyopenssl
Summary: PyOpenSSL Use-After-Free vulnerability
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:H/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:H
Affected Versions: >=0, <17.5.0
Fix Version: 17.5.0
Details: It was discovered that pyOpenSSL incorrectly handled memory when handling X509 objects. A remote attacker could use this issue to cause pyOpenSSL to crash, resulting in a denial of service, or possibly execute arbitrary code. This attack appears to be exploitable via Depends on the calling application and if it retains a reference to the memory. This vulnerability appears to have been fixed in 17.5.0.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-vp96-hxj8-p424
Package: pyopenssl
Summary: pyOpenSSL allows TLS connection bypass via unhandled callback exception in set_tlsext_servername_callback
Severity: UNKNOWN
Affected Versions: >=0.14.0, <26.0.0
Fix Version: 26.0.0
Details: If a user provided callback to `set_tlsext_servername_callback` raised an unhandled exception, this would result in a connection being accepted. If a user was relying on this callback for any security-sensitive behavior, this could allow bypassing it.

Unhandled exceptions now result in rejecting the connection.

Credit to **Leury Castillo** for reporting this issue.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-5wmx-573v-2qwq
Package: markdown
Summary: Python-Markdown has an Uncaught Exception
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:N/A:H
Affected Versions: >=0, <3.8.1
Fix Version: 3.8.1
Details: Python-Markdown version 3.8 contain a vulnerability where malformed HTML-like sequences can cause html.parser.HTMLParser to raise an unhandled AssertionError during Markdown parsing. Because Python-Markdown does not catch this exception, any application that processes attacker-controlled Markdown may crash. This enables remote, unauthenticated Denial of Service in web applications, documentation systems, CI/CD pipelines, and any service that renders untrusted Markdown. The issue was acknowledged
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---

Advisory ID: GHSA-9w8r-397f-prfh
Package: pygments
Summary: Infinite Loop in Pygments
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:N/A:H
Affected Versions: >=1.5, <2.7.4
Fix Version: 2.7.4
Details: An infinite loop in SMLLexer in Pygments versions 1.5 to 2.7.3 may lead to denial of service when performing syntax highlighting of a Standard ML (SML) source file, as demonstrated by input that only contains the "exception" keyword.

--- PYPI ADVISORY ---
Advisory ID: GHSA-pq64-v7f5-gqh8
Package: pygments
Summary: Pygments vulnerable to Regular Expression Denial of Service (ReDoS)
Severity: CVSS:3.1/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:N/S:U/C:N/I:N/A:H
Affected Versions: >=1.1, <2.7.4
Fix Version: 2.7.4
Details: In pygments 1.1+, fixed in 2.7.4, the lexers used to parse programming languages rely heavily on regular expressions. Some of the regular expressions have exponential or cubic worst-case complexity and are vulnerable to ReDoS. By crafting malicious input, an attacker can cause a denial of service.
--- END PYPI ADVISORY ---
